<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2a0a38fc-f5bb-4442-a2ac-e7a5b1ee5408'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer10277208060699723498">Its always refreshing to read for a female writer, not only I'm a woman and it makes me proud of how good the writer is but also its different to read for a woman, as we tend to notice lots of details men mostly don’t see, or ignore. And of course it’s a different style of writing.   <span id="freeText10277208060699723498" style="display:none">Its always refreshing to read for a female writer, not only I'm a woman and it makes me proud of how good the writer is but also its different to read for a woman, as we tend to notice lots of details men mostly don’t see, or ignore. And of course it’s a different style of writing. This is basically a horror novel, or lets say it has supernatural/metaphysical elements cause some writers or critics don’t like the word horror or categorizing a work of art at all… <br />Anyway, reading this really big novel was – again – refreshing. The diaries or the letters from a mother to her unborn child (at first) was very moving, not only the sentimentality of the idea but how it summarized a period of time, the feelings of the main character (Rana) and pointed out at so many issues in the society. Starting from marriage, and family, to the relationships between people in general, healthy or not. Lets count them…, no, you'll get it when you read, and if you already did then you do know.<br />I'd like to say that this isn’t a novel, not only a novel but its rather a social study, after all some writers reflect and expose the society in their works, and this work does that exactly. <br /><br />(The rest of the review can be found at --&gt; (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewingalltime.blogspot.com/2012/10/the-dystopian-world-of-sherin-hanaey.html">http://reviewingalltime.blogspot.com/...</a>) DO NOT COPY THE REVIEW, SHARE IT! </span>

  <span id="freeText9949586379406385874" style="display:none">I finished it last night and i swear i wasn't able to put it down!!<br />3.8 stars actually.<br /><br /><br />و دي هي الملاحظات الكتبتها وأنا بقرأه:<br /><br />- A page turner this book is. You sit thinking you'll read a bit and suddenly you realize you just read 100 pages!<br /><br />- All my previous experiences with diary weren't successful, meaning other books that i read that were written as a diary were awful! But i quiet liked this one. <br /><br />-a great point, a good message, and the story is told in a good way!<br /><br />- The ending is beautiful. It made me smile. I really appreciate the notsohappy but satisfying ending!<br /><br />بقيت قاعدة أتخيل الخيوط الماسكانا دي ولوين بتمد، و أنا ممتنة لشيرين هنائي لأنها اتكلمت عن الموضوع ده بتوسع وطيقت الموضوع في قصتها<br /><br />الما عجبني: <br /><br />I wanted to point out that i didn't like that Rana was looking for a man the whole time, that her main goal in life was to find a male that she could throw herself at. I'm glad the author showed us that Rana was a doll too who is being controlled. Also, Rana makes many not-so-correct decision and she doesn't think about the consequences or result in the long term. She is no heroine but maybe she portrays a common type of women. But i feel it was important to have her as a protagonist and see things from her point if view. She was not the only character with flaws though, (Zain for instance is a horrible person with double-standers if you take time to reflect on what he has done) but because Rana is the main character i wanted her to be more likable<br /><br />حسيت انها بتصور النساء على انهم كائنات سخيفة ما همها الا الونسة و الاقاويل والجمال و البحث عن راجل يحميهم و يستظلوا بيه<br />بس كمان بترجع الكاتبة بعد كل تصوير لموقف من المواقف دي بتقول ما معناه انه "لكن ده ما صح" فهي كأنها زي ما حباب قالت لي لما ناقشتها في الفكرة دي "بتعري لينا الشخصيات و تكشف عيوبهم" <br /><br />شي ثاني هو غضب الكاتبة من المراهقين (هي في حاجات صح كلامها فيها. مثال: عيد الحب و الدبدوب) لكن أنا لقيت نفسي ما بوافقها على كل شي و حسيتها احيانا ممكن تكون شوية judgmental وشايفة انه شباب الزمن ده ما نافعين.<br /><br /> حسيت إنه ده ما رعب، الكتاب مفروض يكون مندرج تحت Supernatural مش رعب<br /><br />حسيت اني محتارة في بعض الأحداث وما كان واضح شديد كل شي كيف حصل</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1180913223" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7840586888763980350">Omg I'm finally done with this book. at some point I just wanted it to end because of its complexity. Also I sometimes felt that I'm taken to another book she didn't integrate the facts with the story properly. I didn't like how Rana had to in close her sorrows as a wife ... she didn't express herself ... One of the reasons why her marriage collapsed ... And Zain was a typical man if she doesn't talk and I'm providing her with material stuff she is fine .. basically they don't understand that ma</span>
  <span id="freeText7840586888763980350" style="display:none">Omg I'm finally done with this book. at some point I just wanted it to end because of its complexity. Also I sometimes felt that I'm taken to another book she didn't integrate the facts with the story properly. I didn't like how Rana had to in close her sorrows as a wife ... she didn't express herself ... One of the reasons why her marriage collapsed ... And Zain was a typical man if she doesn't talk and I'm providing her with material stuff she is fine .. basically they don't understand that material is not everything. I had mixed feelings after she fleed away from her husband. no comment about Zain 2nd marriage. I like the main idea of smokey threads and how the humanity is being controlled by some ideas and how they go with the flow like soulless dolls ... they are satisfied with what's given no one questions anything from what's going around ... As long as they are living and they are enjoying life * NOT*. I think that's what makes people built the selfishness into themselves. <br /><br />Didn't like the Rana &amp; Ramzi relationship because each one had different feeling towards the other part. <br /><br />The blue little dude character contradicted itself a lot. I could understand that he wanted Ramzi to die because he wanted Rana to investigate by herself so he can get what he wants. but I don't understand why he wanted everyone dead in the end ... why he helps Athr and then he wanted him dead ... Just to get his body back ? and help the organization ? or kill the madam ahhhh it's complicated I just didn't understand his part in the end <br /><br />The novel is not horror at all. The ending was smokey and incomplete. I thought she had to explain what happened with the rest of the main characters.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+pzAkD/SgT6JHHgfsUVTOmRpE7Gqzg4B9A1fSpIn1FbWdGRY26GkGuOgXyc1gtvrLTjk07VFEThmiGLFMhBA/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pRCmZYjgari613ECbAK1AJZAb83eV6d7bhdK/2IjbXqJ+AKtbJNPnNBrVjroxT3R3xGYr8HcuEL8kndwwhT50A==')})
  }
